<p><i><b>Jurassic Park</b></i> is a 1993 American <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction_film" title="Science fiction film">science fiction</a> <a href="/wiki/Adventure_film" title="Adventure film">adventure film</a> directed by <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a>. It is the first installment of the <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park" title="Jurassic Park"><i>Jurassic Park</i> franchise</a>. It is based on the 1990 <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_(novel)" title="Jurassic Park (novel)">novel of the same name</a> by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Crichton" title="Michael Crichton">Michael Crichton</a>, with a screenplay written by Crichton and <a href="/wiki/David_Koepp" title="David Koepp">David Koepp</a>. The film centers on the fictional Isla Nublar, an islet located off <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>'s Pacific Coast, near <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>, where a billionaire philanthropist and a small team of genetic scientists have created a <a href="/wiki/Animal_theme_park" title="Animal theme park">wildlife park</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cloning" title="Cloning">cloned</a> <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaurs</a>.</p>
<p>Before Crichton's novel was published, four studios put in bids for the film rights. With the backing of <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" title="Universal Studios">Universal Studios</a>, Spielberg acquired the rights for $1.5 million before publication in 1990; Crichton was hired for an additional $500,000 to adapt the novel for the screen. David Koepp wrote the final draft, which left out much of the novel's exposition and violence and made numerous changes to the characters. Filming took place in California and Hawaii between August and November 1992, and post-production rolled until May 1993, supervised by Spielberg in Poland as he filmed <i><a href="/wiki/Schindler%27s_List" title="Schindler's List">Schindler's List</a></i> . The dinosaurs were created with groundbreaking <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated imagery</a> by <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic" title="Industrial Light &amp; Magic">Industrial Light &amp; Magic</a> and with life-sized <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animatronic" title="Animatronic">animatronic</a> dinosaurs built by <a href="/wiki/Stan_Winston" title="Stan Winston">Stan Winston</a>'s team. To showcase the film's sound design, which included a mixture of various animal noises for the dinosaur roars, Spielberg invested in the creation of <a href="/wiki/DTS_(sound_system)" title="DTS (sound system)">DTS</a>, a company specializing in digital <a href="/wiki/Surround_sound" title="Surround sound">surround sound</a> formats.</p>
<p>Following an extensive $65 million marketing campaign, which included licensing deals with 100 companies, <i>Jurassic Park</i> grossed over $900 million worldwide in its original theatrical run. It surpassed Spielberg's 1982 film <i><a href="/wiki/E.T._the_Extra-Terrestrial" title="E.T. the Extra-Terrestrial">E.T. the Extra-Terrestrial</a></i> to become the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">highest-grossing film</a> until <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> (1997). <i>Jurassic Park</i> was well received by critics, who praised its special effects and Spielberg's direction but criticized the script. The film won more than 20 awards (including 3 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a>), mostly for its visual effects. Following a re-release in 2011 and made $786,021 and again 2013 <a href="/wiki/3D_film" title="3D film">3D</a> to celebrate its 20th anniversary, <i>Jurassic Park</i> became the 17th film with total grosses of more than $1 billion. It is the 14th-highest-grossing film worldwide, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States#Not_adjusted_for_inflation" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">16th-highest-grossing film in North America</a> (unadjusted for inflation), and the highest-grossing film released by Universal and directed by Spielberg. <i>Jurassic Park</i> is considered by many to be one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_considered_the_best" title="List of films considered the best">greatest films of the 1990s</a> and in some cases of all-time, as well as a landmark in the vector of visual effects regarding its computer-generated imagery and animatronics.</p>
<p><i>Jurassic Park</i> was followed by two sequels, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lost_World:_Jurassic_Park" title="The Lost World: Jurassic Park">The Lost World: Jurassic Park</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_III" title="Jurassic Park III">Jurassic Park III</a></i>, both of which were box office successes but received mixed critical responses. A third sequel, <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_World" title="Jurassic World">Jurassic World</a>,</i> is set for release on June 12, 2015.</p>
<p></p>
