<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Hammond_(Jurassic_Park_character)" title="John Hammond (Jurassic Park character)">John Hammond</a> (<a href="/wiki/Richard_Attenborough" title="Richard Attenborough">Richard Attenborough</a>), the founder and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Biological_engineering" title="Biological engineering">bioengineering</a> company InGen, has created a <a href="/wiki/Animal_theme_park" title="Animal theme park">theme park</a> called Jurassic Park on Isla Nublar, a tropical island in an isolated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American" title="Central American">Central American</a> location populated with cloned <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaurs</a>. After a park worker is killed by a <i><a href="/wiki/Velociraptor" title="Velociraptor">Velociraptor</a></i>, the park's investors, represented by lawyer Donald Gennaro (<a href="/wiki/Martin_Ferrero" title="Martin Ferrero">Martin Ferrero</a>), demand that experts visit the park and certify it as safe. Gennaro invites the mathematician Ian Malcolm (<a href="/wiki/Jeff_Goldblum" title="Jeff Goldblum">Jeff Goldblum</a>) while Hammond invites paleontologist Dr. Alan Grant (<a href="/wiki/Sam_Neill" title="Sam Neill">Sam Neill</a>) and paleobotanist Dr. Ellie Sattler (<a href="/wiki/Laura_Dern" title="Laura Dern">Laura Dern</a>). Upon arrival, the group is stunned to see three <i><a href="/wiki/Brachiosaurus" title="Brachiosaurus">Brachiosaurus</a></i> and a herd of <i><a href="/wiki/Parasaurolophus" title="Parasaurolophus">Parasaurolophus</a></i> in the distance.</p>
<p>At the visitor center, the group learns during a laboratory tour that the cloning was accomplished by extracting the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_DNA" title="Ancient DNA">DNA of dinosaurs</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mosquito" title="Mosquito">mosquitoes</a> that had been preserved in <a href="/wiki/Amber" title="Amber">amber</a>. The DNA strands were incomplete, so DNA from frogs was used to fill in the gaps. The dinosaurs were all cloned genetically as females in order to prevent breeding.</p>
<p>The group is then joined by Hammond's grandchildren, Lex and Tim Murphy (<a href="/wiki/Ariana_Richards" title="Ariana Richards">Ariana Richards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Mazzello" title="Joseph Mazzello">Joseph Mazzello</a>) for a tour of the park, while Hammond oversees the trip from the park's control room. The tour does not go as planned, with the dinosaurs failing to appear and a <i><a href="/wiki/Triceratops" title="Triceratops">Triceratops</a></i> becoming ill. As a tropical storm approaches Isla Nublar, the tour is cut short. Most of the park employees depart on a boat for the mainland and the visitors return to the electric tour vehicles, except Ellie, who stays with the park's veterinarian to study the Triceratops.</p>
<p>During the storm, Jurassic Park's computer programmer, Dennis Nedry (<a href="/wiki/Wayne_Knight" title="Wayne Knight">Wayne Knight</a>), who has been bribed by a corporate rival to steal dinosaur embryos, deactivates the park's security system to allow him access to the embryo storage room. The power goes out, and the tour vehicles become stuck. Most of the park's electric fences are deactivated, leading the <i><a href="/wiki/Tyrannosaurus" title="Tyrannosaurus">Tyrannosaurus rex</a></i> to attack the tour group. Grant, Lex, and Tim narrowly escape while the Tyrannosaurus devours Gennaro, injures Malcolm, and pushes one of the vehicles over an embankment. On his way to deliver the embryos to the island's docks, Nedry becomes lost, crashes his Jeep, and is killed by a <i><a href="/wiki/Dilophosaurus" title="Dilophosaurus">Dilophosaurus</a></i>.</p>
<p>Sattler assists the park's game warden, Robert Muldoon (<a href="/wiki/Bob_Peck" title="Bob Peck">Bob Peck</a>), in a search for survivors, but they only find Malcolm before the Tyrannosaurus rex returns. They escape in one of the vehicles. Unable to decipher Nedry's code to reactivate the security system, Hammond and the park's chief engineer Ray Arnold (<a href="/wiki/Samuel_L._Jackson" title="Samuel L. Jackson">Samuel L. Jackson</a>) opt to reboot the entire park's system. The group shuts down the park's grid and retreats to an emergency bunker, while Arnold heads to a maintenance shed to complete the rebooting process. When he fails to return, Sattler and Muldoon head to the shed themselves. They discover the shutdown has deactivated the remaining fences and released the Velociraptors; Muldoon distracts the raptors while Sattler turns the power back on. She discovers Arnold's severed arm and escapes. Soon after, the raptors ambush and kill Muldoon.</p>
<p>Grant, Tim, and Lex discover the broken shells of dinosaur eggs. Grant concludes that the dinosaurs have been breeding, which occurred because they have the genetic coding of frog DNA—<a href="/wiki/African_bullfrog" title="African bullfrog">West African bullfrogs</a> <a href="/wiki/Sequential_hermaphroditism" title="Sequential hermaphroditism">can change their sex in a single-sex environment</a>, making the dinosaurs able to do so as well. On the way back to the visitor center, the trio encounter a herd of <a href="/wiki/Gallimimus" title="Gallimimus">Gallimimus</a>, when suddenly the Tyrannosaurus emerges from nowhere and kills one. Grant, Tim and Lex reach the visitor center, and Grant leaves them there as he goes searching for the others. After finding the bunker, Grant and Sattler head back to the visitor center, where the children battle two Velociraptors. The four head to the control room, where Lex restores full power, allowing the group to call for help. While trying to leave, they are cornered by the raptors but escape when the Tyrannosaurus suddenly appears and kills both raptors. Hammond arrives in a jeep with Malcolm, and the entire group flees together. Before they board a <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">helicopter</a> to leave the island, Grant decides not to endorse the park, a choice with which Hammond concurs.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Jurassic_Park_characters" title="List of Jurassic Park characters">List of Jurassic Park characters</a></div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sam_Neill" title="Sam Neill">Sam Neill</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alan_Grant_(Jurassic_Park)" title="Alan Grant (Jurassic Park)">Dr. Alan Grant</a>, a leading paleontologist.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Laura_Dern" title="Laura Dern">Laura Dern</a> as Dr. Ellie Sattler, a paleobotanist.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jeff_Goldblum" title="Jeff Goldblum">Jeff Goldblum</a> as Dr. Ian Malcolm, a mathematician and chaos theorist.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_Attenborough" title="Richard Attenborough">Richard Attenborough</a> as John Hammond, InGen's billionaire CEO and the park's creator.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ariana_Richards" title="Ariana Richards">Ariana Richards</a> as Alexis "Lex" Murphy, Hammond's granddaughter.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Mazzello" title="Joseph Mazzello">Joseph Mazzello</a> as Timothy "Tim" Murphy, Hammond's grandson.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bob_Peck" title="Bob Peck">Bob Peck</a> as Robert Muldoon, the park's game warden.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Martin_Ferrero" title="Martin Ferrero">Martin Ferrero</a> as Donald Gennaro, a lawyer who represents Hammond's concerned investors.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wayne_Knight" title="Wayne Knight">Wayne Knight</a> as Dennis Nedry, the disgruntled architect of the park's computer systems.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Samuel_L._Jackson" title="Samuel L. Jackson">Samuel L. Jackson</a> as Ray Arnold, the park's chief engineer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cameron_Thor" title="Cameron Thor">Cameron Thor</a> as Dr. Lewis Dodgson, the head of InGen's rival, BioSyn.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miguel_Sandoval" title="Miguel Sandoval">Miguel Sandoval</a> as Juanito Rostagno, the <i>Mano de Dios</i> amber mine's proprietor.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gerald_R._Molen" title="Gerald R. Molen">Gerald R. Molen</a> as Dr. Gerry Harding, the park's veterinarian.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BD_Wong" title="BD Wong">BD Wong</a> as Dr. Henry Wu, the park's chief geneticist.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_Kiley" title="Richard Kiley">Richard Kiley</a> as himself, providing audio narration for the park's main tour.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greg_Burson" title="Greg Burson">Greg Burson</a> as Mr. D.N.A., the animated DNA strand that explains the miracle of cloning.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MichaelCrichton_2.jpg"><img alt="Michael Crichton wearing a suit." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="919" data-file-width="701" height="288" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/MichaelCrichton_2.jpg/220px-MichaelCrichton_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/MichaelCrichton_2.jpg/330px-MichaelCrichton_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/MichaelCrichton_2.jpg/440px-MichaelCrichton_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MichaelCrichton_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Michael_Crichton" title="Michael Crichton">Michael Crichton</a>'s book attracted the attention of director Steven Spielberg even before publishing. The author was also responsible for the film's first scripts.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Michael_Crichton" title="Michael Crichton">Michael Crichton</a> originally conceived a <a href="/wiki/Screenplay" title="Screenplay">screenplay</a> about a graduate student who recreates a dinosaur; he continued to wrestle with his fascination with dinosaurs and cloning until he began writing the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_(novel)" title="Jurassic Park (novel)">Jurassic Park</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Even before publication, <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a> learned of the novel in October 1989 while he and Crichton were discussing a screenplay that would become the television series <i><a href="/wiki/ER_(TV_series)" title="ER (TV series)">ER</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcbride_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-mcbride-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Spielberg considered that what really fascinated him was that <i>Jurassic Park</i> was "a really credible look at how dinosaurs might someday be brought back alongside modern mankind", going beyond a simple monster movie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dawn_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-dawn-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Before the book was published, Crichton demanded a non-negotiable fee of $1.5 million as well as a substantial percentage of the gross. <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Burton" title="Tim Burton">Tim Burton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Pictures" title="Columbia Pictures">Columbia Pictures</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Donner" title="Richard Donner">Richard Donner</a>, and <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Dante" title="Joe Dante">Joe Dante</a> bid for the rights,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcbride_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-mcbride-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> but <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" title="Universal Studios">Universal Studios</a> eventually acquired them in May 1990 for Spielberg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Production_notes_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Production_notes-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> After completing <i><a href="/wiki/Hook_(film)" title="Hook (film)">Hook</a></i>, Spielberg wanted to film <i><a href="/wiki/Schindler%27s_List" title="Schindler's List">Schindler's List</a></i>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_Corporation_of_America" title="Music Corporation of America">Music Corporation of America</a> (then Universal Pictures' parent company) president <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sid_Sheinberg" title="Sid Sheinberg">Sid Sheinberg</a> gave a green light to the film on the condition that Spielberg made <i>Jurassic Park</i> first.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcbride_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-mcbride-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> The director later declared that by choosing a creature-driven thriller, "I was really just trying to make a good sequel to <i><a href="/wiki/Jaws_(film)" title="Jaws (film)">Jaws</a></i>, on land."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>To create the dinosaurs, Spielberg at first thought of hiring <a href="/wiki/Bob_Gurr" title="Bob Gurr">Bob Gurr</a>, who designed a giant mechanical <a href="/wiki/King_Kong" title="King Kong">King Kong</a> for <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios_Hollywood" title="Universal Studios Hollywood">Universal Studios Hollywood</a>'s <a href="/wiki/King_Kong_Encounter" title="King Kong Encounter">King Kong Encounter</a>. Upon considering that the life-sized dinosaurs would be too expensive and not all convincing, Spielberg instead decided to look after the best effects supervisors in Hollywood. Brought in were <a href="/wiki/Stan_Winston" title="Stan Winston">Stan Winston</a> to create the <a href="/wiki/Animatronics" title="Animatronics">animatronic</a> dinosaurs, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Tippett" title="Phil Tippett">Phil Tippett</a> to create <a href="/wiki/Go_motion" title="Go motion">go motion</a> dinosaurs for <a href="/wiki/Long_shot" title="Long shot">long shots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Lantieri" title="Michael Lantieri">Michael Lantieri</a> to supervise the on-set effects, and <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Muren" title="Dennis Muren">Dennis Muren</a> of <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic" title="Industrial Light &amp; Magic">Industrial Light &amp; Magic</a> to do the <a href="/wiki/Digital_compositing" title="Digital compositing">digital compositing</a>. Paleontologist <a href="/wiki/Jack_Horner_(paleontologist)" title="Jack Horner (paleontologist)">Jack Horner</a> supervised the designs, to help fulfill Spielberg's desire to portray the dinosaurs as animals rather than monsters. This led to the entry of certain concepts about dinosaurs, such as the theory that dinosaurs <a href="/wiki/Origin_of_birds" title="Origin of birds">evolved into birds</a> and had very little in common with lizards. One of the first consequences was the removal of the raptors' flicking tongues in Tippett's early <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animatics" title="Animatics">animatics</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earl_doc_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Earl_doc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> as Horner complained it was implausible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-French-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Winston's department created fully detailed models of the dinosaurs before molding <a href="/wiki/Latex" title="Latex">latex</a> skins, which were fitted over complex robotics. Tippett created stop-motion animatics of both the raptors in the kitchen and the <i>Tyrannosaurus</i> attacking the car. But despite go motion's attempts at <a href="/wiki/Motion_blur" title="Motion blur">motion blurs</a>, Spielberg still found the end results unsatisfactory in terms of working in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live-action" title="Live-action">live-action</a> feature film. Muren declared to Spielberg that he thought the dinosaurs could be built through <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated imagery</a>, and the director asked him to prove it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earl_doc_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Earl_doc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> ILM animators <a href="/wiki/Mark_A.Z._Dipp%C3%A9" title="Mark A.Z. Dippé">Mark Dippé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Williams_(animator)" title="Steve Williams (animator)">Steve Williams</a> developed a computer-generated walk cycle for the <i>T. rex</i> skeleton, and were approved to do more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> When Spielberg and Tippett saw an animatic of the <i>T. rex</i> chasing a herd of <i>Gallimimus</i>, Spielberg said, "You're out of a job," to which Tippett replied, "Don't you mean extinct?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earl_doc_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-Earl_doc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Spielberg later wrote both the animatic and his dialogue between him and Tippett into the script, as a conversation between Malcolm and Grant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gallies_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-gallies-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Although no go motion was used, Tippett and his animators were still used by the production to supervise dinosaur movement. Tippett acted as a consultant regarding dinosaur anatomy, and his stop motion animators were re-trained as computer animators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earl_doc_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-Earl_doc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The animatics made by Tippett's team were also used along with the <a href="/wiki/Storyboard" title="Storyboard">storyboards</a> as a reference for what would be shot during the action sequences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-pre-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> ILM's artists were sent to private tours to the local animal park so they could study large animals — rhinos, elephants, alligators, and giraffes — up close, and also received <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mime" title="Mime">mime</a> classes for understanding movements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-back_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-back-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing">Writing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Writing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Universal paid Crichton a further $500,000 to adapt his own novel,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> which he had finished by the time Spielberg was filming <i><a href="/wiki/Hook_(film)" title="Hook (film)">Hook</a></i>. Crichton noted that because the book was "fairly long" his script only had about 10 to 20 percent of the novel's content; scenes were dropped for budgetary and practical reasons, and despite the gory descriptions, the violence was toned down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Biodrowski_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Biodrowski-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malia_Scotch_Marmo" title="Malia Scotch Marmo">Malia Scotch Marmo</a> began a script rewrite in October 1991 over a five-month period, merging Ian Malcolm with Alan Grant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As Spielberg wanted another writer to rework the script, Universal president <a href="/wiki/Casey_Silver" title="Casey Silver">Casey Silver</a> recommended him <a href="/wiki/David_Koepp" title="David Koepp">David Koepp</a>, co-writer of <i><a href="/wiki/Death_Becomes_Her" title="Death Becomes Her">Death Becomes Her</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Koepp started afresh from Marmo's draft, and used Spielberg's idea of a cartoon shown to the visitors to remove much of the exposition that fills Crichton's novel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-koepp_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-koepp-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> While Koepp tried to avert excessive character detail "because whenever they started talking about their personal lives, you couldn't care less",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> he tried to flesh out the characters and make for a more colorful cast, with moments such as Malcolm flirting with Satler leading to Grant's jealousy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dawn_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-dawn-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Some <a href="/wiki/Characterization" title="Characterization">characterizations</a> were changed from the novel. Hammond went from a ruthless businessman to a kindly old man, because Spielberg identified with Hammond's obsession with showmanship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lack_of_story.3F_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-lack_of_story.3F-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> He also switched the characters of Tim and Lex; in the book, Tim is aged eleven and interested in computers, and Lex is only seven or eight and interested in sports. Spielberg did this because he wanted to work with the younger Joseph Mazzello, and it also allowed him to introduce the sub-plot of Lex's adolescent crush on Grant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-casting_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-casting-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Koepp changed Grant's relationship with the children, making him hostile to them initially to allow for more character development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcbride_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-mcbride-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Two scenes from the book were excised, with Spielberg removing the opening sequence with <i><a href="/wiki/Procompsognathus" title="Procompsognathus">Procompsognathus</a></i> attacking young children as he found it too horrific,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> and Koepp cutting for budgetary reasons the <i>T. rex</i> chasing Grant and the children down a river before being tranquilized by Muldoon. Both parts eventually saw inclusion in the film sequels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-koepp_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-koepp-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Spielberg suggested the addition of the scene where the <i>T. rex</i> pursues a jeep, which at first would only have the characters driving away after listening to the dinosaur's footsteps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Filming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jurassic_Park_car.jpg"><img alt="A utility car painted in green, yellow and red colors in a jungle park environment." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Jurassic_Park_car.jpg/220px-Jurassic_Park_car.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Jurassic_Park_car.jpg/330px-Jurassic_Park_car.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Jurassic_Park_car.jpg/440px-Jurassic_Park_car.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jurassic_Park_car.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Replica of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Explorer" title="Ford Explorer">Ford Explorers</a> featured in the film at <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios_Japan" title="Universal Studios Japan">Universal Studios Japan</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After 25 months of pre-production, filming began on August 24, 1992, on the <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaiian</a> island of <a href="/wiki/Kauai" title="Kauai">Kaua<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> While <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a> was considered as a location given it is the story's setting, Spielberg's concerns on infrastructure and accessibility made him choose a place where he had already worked before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dawn_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-dawn-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> The three-week shoot involved various daytime exteriors for Isla Nublar's forests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Production_notes_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Production_notes-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> On September 11, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Iniki" title="Hurricane Iniki">Hurricane Iniki</a> passed directly over Kaua<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i, which caused the crew to lose a day of shooting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Several of the storm scenes from the movie are actual footage shot during the hurricane. The scheduled shoot of the <i>Gallimimus</i> chase was moved to <a href="/wiki/Kualoa_Ranch" title="Kualoa Ranch">Kualoa Ranch</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Oahu" title="Oahu">Oahu</a> and one of the beginning scenes had to be created by digitally animating a still shot of scenery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gallies_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-gallies-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The opening scene was shot in Haiku, on the island of <a href="/wiki/Maui" title="Maui">Maui</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haiku_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-haiku-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> with additional scenes being filmed on the "forbidden island" of <a href="/wiki/Niihau" title="Niihau">Niihau</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greenie_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-greenie-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> By mid-September, the crew moved back to California,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earl_doc_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-Earl_doc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> to shoot the raptors in the kitchen at Stage 24 of the Universal studio lot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Production_notes_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Production_notes-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Given the kitchen set was filled with reflective surfaces, cinematographer <a href="/wiki/Dean_Cundey" title="Dean Cundey">Dean Cundey</a> had to carefully plan the illumination while also using black cloths to hide the light reflections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-pre-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The crew also shot on Stage 23 for the scenes involving the power supply, before going on location to <a href="/wiki/Red_Rock_Canyon_State_Park_(California)" title="Red Rock Canyon State Park (California)">Red Rock Canyon</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a> dig scenes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-location_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-location-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The crew returned to Universal to shoot Grant's rescue of Tim, using a fifty-foot prop with hydraulic wheels for the car fall, and the <i>Brachiosaurus</i> encounter. The crew filmed scenes for the Park's labs and control room, which used animations for the computers lent from <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Graphics" title="Silicon Graphics">Silicon Graphics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-triple_cite_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-triple_cite-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> While Crichton's book features <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a> cars on Jurassic Park, Spielberg got a deal with the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford Motor Company</a>, who provided seven <a href="/wiki/Ford_Explorer" title="Ford Explorer">Ford Explorers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shone_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-shone-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> The Explorers were modified by ILM's crew and veteran customizer <a href="/wiki/George_Barris_(auto_customizer)" title="George Barris (auto customizer)">George Barris</a> to create the illusion that they were <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_car" title="Autonomous car">autonomous cars</a> by hiding the driver in the car's trunk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Barris also customized the <a href="/wiki/Jeep_Wrangler" title="Jeep Wrangler">Jeep Wranglers</a> featured in the production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The crew moved to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Studios" title="Warner Bros. Studios">Warner Bros. Studios</a>' Stage 16 to shoot the <i>T. rex</i> '​s attack on the SUVs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-triple_cite_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-triple_cite-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Shooting proved frustrating due to water soaking the foam rubber skin of the animatronic dinosaur, which caused the animatronic <i>T. rex</i> to shake and quiver from the extra weight when the foam absorbed the water. This forced Stan Winston's crew to dry the model with <a href="/wiki/Chamois_leather" title="Chamois leather">shammys</a> between takes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-big_fan_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-big_fan-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> On the set, Malcolm distracting the dinosaur with a flare was included at Jeff Goldblum's suggestion, as he felt a heroic action was better than going by the script, where like Gennaro, Malcolm would get scared and run away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-pre-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The ripples in the glass of water caused by the <i>T. rex</i> '​s footsteps was inspired by Spielberg listening to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth,_Wind_and_Fire" title="Earth, Wind and Fire">Earth, Wind and Fire</a> in his car, and the vibrations the bass rhythm caused. Lantieri was unsure of how to create the shot until the night before filming, when he put a glass of water on a guitar he was playing, which achieved the concentric circles in the water Spielberg wanted. The next morning, guitar strings were put inside the car and a man on the floor plucked the strings to achieve the effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Back at Universal, the crew filmed scenes with the <i>Dilophosaurus</i> on Stage 27. Finally, the shoot finished on Stage 12, with the climactic chases with the raptors in the Park's computer rooms and Visitor's Center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dilo_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-dilo-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Spielberg changed the climax to bring back the <i>T. rex</i>, abandoning the original ending in which Grant uses a platform machine to maneuver a raptor into a fossil tyrannosaur's jaws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The scene which already had the juxtaposition of live dinosaurs in a museum filled with fossils, while also destroying the bones, now also had an ending where the <i>T. rex</i> saved the protagonists, and afterwards did what Spielberg described as a "King Kong roar" while an ironic banner reading "When Dinosaurs Ruled the Earth" flew.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-pre-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The film wrapped twelve days ahead of schedule on November 30,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> and within days, editor <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kahn_(film_editor)" title="Michael Kahn (film editor)">Michael Kahn</a> had a rough cut ready, allowing Spielberg to go ahead with filming <i><a href="/wiki/Schindler%27s_List" title="Schindler's List">Schindler's List</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-production">Post-production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Post-production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Special effects work continued on the film, with Tippett's unit adjusting to new technology with Dinosaur Input Devices:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIGCHI_Dinosaur_Input_Device_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-SIGCHI_Dinosaur_Input_Device-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> models which fed information into the computers to allow themselves to animate the characters like stop motion puppets. In addition, they acted out scenes with the raptors and <i>Gallimimus</i>. As well as the computer-generated dinosaurs, ILM also created elements such as water splashing and digital face replacement for Ariana Richards' stunt double.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earl_doc_8-5"><a href="#cite_note-Earl_doc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Compositing the dinosaurs onto the live action scenes took around an hour. Rendering the dinosaurs often took two to four hours per frame, and rendering the <i>T. rex</i> in the rain even took six hours per frame.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Silicon_Valley_ACM_Siggraph_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Silicon_Valley_ACM_Siggraph-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Spielberg monitored their progress from <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> during the filming of <i>Schindler's List</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hopefully_the_only_double_page_ref_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hopefully_the_only_double_page_ref-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> having teleconferences four times a week with ILM's crew. The director described working simultaneously in two vastly different productions as "a bipolar experience", where he used "every ounce of intuition on <i>Schindler's List</i> and every ounce of craft in <i>Jurassic Park</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-next_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-next-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Along with the digital effects, Spielberg wanted the film to be the first with digital sound. He funded the creation of <a href="/wiki/DTS_(sound_system)" title="DTS (sound system)">DTS</a>, which would allow audiences to "really hear the movie the way it was intended to be heard".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-next_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-next-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The sound effects crew, supervised by <a href="/wiki/George_Lucas" title="George Lucas">George Lucas</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> were finished by the end of April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the_end_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-the_end-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Sound designer <a href="/wiki/Gary_Rydstrom" title="Gary Rydstrom">Gary Rydstrom</a> considered it a fun process, given the film had all kinds of noise - animal sounds, rain, gunshots, car crashes - and at times no music. During the process, Spielberg would take the weekends to fly from Poland to <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, where he would meet Rydstrom to see the sound progress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-next_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-next-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Jurassic Park</i> was finally completed on May 28, 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the_end_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-the_end-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_(film_score)" title="Jurassic Park (film score)">Jurassic Park (film score)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Williams_tux.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/John_Williams_tux.jpg/200px-John_Williams_tux.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/John_Williams_tux.jpg/300px-John_Williams_tux.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/John_Williams_tux.jpg/400px-John_Williams_tux.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_Williams_tux.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
John Williams</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Composer <a href="/wiki/John_Williams" title="John Williams">John Williams</a> began scoring the film at the end of February, and it was recorded a month later. John Neufeld and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Courage" title="Alexander Courage">Alexander Courage</a> provided the score's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orchestrations" title="Orchestrations">orchestrations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the_end_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-the_end-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Like with another Spielberg film he scored, <i><a href="/wiki/Close_Encounters_of_the_Third_Kind" title="Close Encounters of the Third Kind">Close Encounters of the Third Kind</a></i>, Williams felt he needed to write "pieces that would convey a sense of 'awe' and fascination" given it dealt with the "overwhelming happiness and excitement" that would emerge from seeing live dinosaurs. In turn more suspenseful scenes such as the <i>Tyrannosaurus</i> attack earned frightening themes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_(film_score)" title="Jurassic Park (film score)">first soundtrack album</a> was released on May 25, 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> For the 20th anniversary of the release of the film, a new soundtrack was issued for <a href="/wiki/Music_download" title="Music download">digital download</a> on April 9, 2013 including four bonus tracks personally selected by Williams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dinosaurs_on_screen">Dinosaurs on screen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Dinosaurs on screen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:StanWinstonTRex.jpg"><img alt="A life-sized Tyrannosaurus robotic model, with hydraulics  where the dinosaur's feet would be, touches a car in a movie set." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="189" data-file-width="315" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ea/StanWinstonTRex.jpg/250px-StanWinstonTRex.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/ea/StanWinstonTRex.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/ea/StanWinstonTRex.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:StanWinstonTRex.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The life-sized animatronic <i>Tyrannosaurus</i> on the set. It is the largest sculpture ever made by Stan Winston Studio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_extinct_genera_in_Jurassic_Park" title="List of extinct genera in Jurassic Park">List of extinct genera in Jurassic Park</a></div>
<p>Despite the title of the film referencing the <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a> period, most of the dinosaurs featured did not exist until the <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> period, with the exception of <i>Brachiosaurus</i> and <i>Dilophosaurus</i>, both of which lived in the Jurassic period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dinomania_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-dinomania-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The screenplay acknowledges this when Dr. Grant describes the ferocity of the <i>Velociraptor</i> to a young boy, saying "Try to imagine yourself in the Cretaceous period..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><i>Tyrannosaurus</i> was acknowledged by Spielberg as "the star of the movie", even leading him to rewrite the ending to feature the <i>T. rex</i> for fear of disappointing the audience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earl_doc_8-6"><a href="#cite_note-Earl_doc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Winston's animatronic <i>T. rex</i> stood 20 feet (6.1 m), weighed 17,500 pounds (7,900 kg),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-triple_cite_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-triple_cite-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> and was 40 feet (12 m) long.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-magic_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-magic-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Jack Horner called it "the closest I've ever been to a live dinosaur".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-magic_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-magic-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> While the consulting paleontologists did not have a consensus on the dinosaur's movement, particularly regarding its running capabilities, animator <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steve_Williams_(special_effects_artist)" title="Steve Williams (special effects artist)">Steve Williams</a> decided to "throw physics out the window and create a <i>T. rex</i> that moved at sixty miles per hour even though its hollow bones would have busted if it ran that fast".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> The major reason was the <i>T. rex</i> chasing a jeep, a scene that took two months to finish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the_end_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-the_end-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> The dinosaur is depicted with a vision system based on movement, though later studies indicated the <i>T. rex</i> had <a href="/wiki/Binocular_vision" title="Binocular vision">binocular vision</a> comparable to a <a href="/wiki/Bird_of_prey" title="Bird of prey">bird of prey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Its roar is a baby <a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">elephant</a> mixed with a <a href="/wiki/Tiger" title="Tiger">tiger</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Alligator" title="Alligator">alligator</a>, and its breath is a <a href="/wiki/Whale" title="Whale">whale</a>'s blow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the_end_45-4"><a href="#cite_note-the_end-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> A dog attacking a rope toy was used for the sounds of the <i>T. rex</i> tearing a <i>Gallimimus</i> apart,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earl_doc_8-7"><a href="#cite_note-Earl_doc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> while cut <a href="/wiki/Sequoia_(genus)" title="Sequoia (genus)">sequoias</a> crashing to the ground became the sound of the dinosaur's footsteps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre_12-4"><a href="#cite_note-pre-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Velociraptor</i> has a major role and it is also the main villain. The animal's depiction was not based on the actual dinosaur genus in question (which itself was significantly smaller). Coincidentally, shortly<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> before Jurassic Park's theatre release, the similar <i><a href="/wiki/Utahraptor" title="Utahraptor">Utahraptor</a></i> was discovered, though was proven bigger in appearance than the film's raptors; this prompted Stan Winston to joke, "We made it, then they discovered it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-magic_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-magic-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> For the attack on character Robert Muldoon and some parts of the kitchen scene, the raptors were <a href="/wiki/Suitmation" title="Suitmation">played by men in suits</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dilo_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-dilo-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">Dolphin</a> screams, <a href="/wiki/Walrus" title="Walrus">walruses</a> bellowing, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geese" title="Geese">geese</a> hissing,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earl_doc_8-8"><a href="#cite_note-Earl_doc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Crane_(bird)" title="Crane (bird)">an African crane</a>'s mating call, <a href="/wiki/Tortoise" title="Tortoise">tortoises</a> mating, and human rasps were mixed to formulate various raptor sounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the_end_45-5"><a href="#cite_note-the_end-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vult_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-vult-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Following discoveries made after the film's release, most paleontologists theorized that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dromaeosaur" title="Dromaeosaur">dromaeosaurs</a> like <i>Velociraptor</i> and <i>Deinonychus</i> had feathers. This feature is only included in <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_III" title="Jurassic Park III">Jurassic Park III</a></i> for the male raptors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paul2002_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-paul2002-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Dilophosaurus</i> was also very different from its real-life counterpart, made significantly smaller to make sure audiences did not confuse it with the raptors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Neck_frill" title="Neck frill">neck frill</a> and its ability to spit venom are fictitious. Its vocal sounds were made by combining a <a href="/wiki/Swan" title="Swan">swan</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Hawk" title="Hawk">hawk</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Howler_monkey" title="Howler monkey">howler monkey</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Rattlesnake" title="Rattlesnake">rattlesnake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earl_doc_8-9"><a href="#cite_note-Earl_doc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The animatronic model, nicknamed "Spitter" by Stan Winston's team, was animated by the puppeteers sitting on a trench in the set floor, and used a <a href="/wiki/Paintball" title="Paintball">paintball</a> mechanism to spit the mixture of <a href="/wiki/Methyl_cellulose" title="Methyl cellulose">methacyl</a> and <a href="/wiki/K-Y_Jelly" title="K-Y Jelly">K-Y Jelly</a> that served as venom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Brachiosaurus</i> is the first dinosaur seen by the park's visitors. It is inaccurately depicted as chewing its food, and standing up on its hind legs to browse among the high tree branches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the_end_45-6"><a href="#cite_note-the_end-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> According to artist Andy Schoneberg, the chewing was done to make the animal seem docile, in a way it resembled a cow chewing its cud. The dinosaur's head and upper neck was the largest puppet without hydraulics built for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite scientific evidence of their having limited vocal capabilities, sound designer Gary Rydstrom decided to represent them with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whale_sound" title="Whale sound">whale songs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donkey" title="Donkey">donkey</a> calls to give them a melodic sense of wonder. Penguins were also recorded to be used in the noises of the dinosaurs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the_end_45-7"><a href="#cite_note-the_end-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Triceratops</i> has an extended cameo, being sick with an unidentified disease. Its appearance was a particular logistical nightmare for Stan Winston when Spielberg asked to shoot the animatronic of the sick creature earlier than expected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> The model, operated by eight puppeteers in the Kaua'i set, wound up being the first dinosaur filmed during production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dawn_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-dawn-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Winston also created a baby <i>Triceratops</i> for Ariana Richards to ride in, a scene cut from the film for pacing reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Gary Rydstrom combined the sound of himself breathing into a cardboard tube with the cows near his workplace at <a href="/wiki/Skywalker_Ranch" title="Skywalker Ranch">Skywalker Ranch</a> to create the <i>Triceratops</i> vocals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vult_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-vult-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Gallimimus</i> are featured in a stampede scene where one of them is devoured by the <i>Tyrannosaurus</i>. The <i>Gallimimus</i> was the first dinosaur to receive a digital version, being featured in two ILM tests, first as a herd of skeletons and then fully skinned while pursued by the <i>T. rex</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earl_doc_8-10"><a href="#cite_note-Earl_doc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Its design was based on <a href="/wiki/Ostrich" title="Ostrich">ostriches</a>, and to emphasize the birdlike qualities, the animation focused mostly on the herd than individual animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> As reference for the dinosaurs' run, the animators were filmed running at the ILM parking lot, with plastic pipes standing in as the tree that the <i>Gallimimus</i> jump over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-next_43-3"><a href="#cite_note-next-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The footage even inspired to incorporate an animal falling in its leap as one of the artists crashed making the jump.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-back_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-back-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Horse squeals became the <i>Gallimimus</i> sounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vult_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-vult-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Parasaurolophus</i> appear in the background during the first encounter with the <i>Brachiosaurus</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_and_promotion">Release and promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Release and promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Universal took the lengthy pre-production to carefully plan the <i>Jurassic Park</i> marketing campaign,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shone_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-shone-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> which cost $65 million and had deals with 100 companies to market 1,000 products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> These included <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_video_games" title="Jurassic Park video games">three <i>Jurassic Park</i> video games</a> by <a href="/wiki/Sega" title="Sega">Sega</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Software" title="Ocean Software">Ocean Software</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-games_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-games-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> a toy line by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenner" title="Kenner">Kenner</a> that was distributed by <a href="/wiki/Hasbro" title="Hasbro">Hasbro</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> "<a href="/wiki/Happy_Meal" title="Happy Meal">Dino-Sized meals</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shone_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-shone-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Novelization" title="Novelization">novelization</a> aimed at young children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The film's trailers only gave fleeting glimpses of the dinosaurs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> a tactic journalist Josh Horowitz described as "that old Spielberg <a href="/wiki/Axiom" title="Axiom">axiom</a> of never revealing too much" when Spielberg and director <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bay" title="Michael Bay">Michael Bay</a> did the same for their production of <i><a href="/wiki/Transformers_(film)" title="Transformers (film)">Transformers</a></i> in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> The film was marketed with the <a href="/wiki/Tagline" title="Tagline">tagline</a> "An Adventure 65 Million Years In The Making." This was a joke Spielberg made on set about the genuine, thousands of years old mosquito in amber used for Hammond's walking stick.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The film premiered at the <a href="/wiki/National_Building_Museum" title="National Building Museum">National Building Museum</a> on June 9, 1993, in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> in support of two children's charities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Two days later it opened nationwide, in 2,404 theater locations and an estimated 3,400 screens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opening_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-opening-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Internationally it was equally wide at 3,400 prints.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sh_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-sh-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the film's release, a traveling exhibition called The Dinosaurs of Jurassic Park began, showcasing dinosaur skeletons and film props.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Jurassic Park</i> was broadcast on television for the first time on May 7, 1995, following the April 26 airing of <i>The Making of Jurassic Park</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Some 68.12 million people tuned in to watch, garnering <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> a 36 percent share of all available viewers that night. <i>Jurassic Park</i> was the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_ratings" title="Nielsen ratings">highest-rated</a> theatrical film broadcast on television by any network since the April 1987 airing of <i><a href="/wiki/Trading_Places" title="Trading Places">Trading Places</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Huff_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Huff-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> In June–July 1995 the film was aired a number of times on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turner_Network_Television" title="Turner Network Television">TNT</a> network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Huff_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Huff-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatrical_re-releases">Theatrical re-releases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Theatrical re-releases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jurassic_Park_3D.jpg"><img alt='A car approaches a gate adorned with the Jurassic Park logo. Atop the gate is a text reading "3D", and at the bottom of the poster, the release date "04.05.13".' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="466" data-file-width="295" height="348" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c7/Jurassic_Park_3D.jpg/220px-Jurassic_Park_3D.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/c7/Jurassic_Park_3D.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/c7/Jurassic_Park_3D.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jurassic_Park_3D.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The theatrical poster for the 3D re-release of <i>Jurassic Park</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In anticipation to the Blu-ray release, <i>Jurassic Park</i> had a <a href="/wiki/Digital_cinema" title="Digital cinema">digital print</a> released in UK cinemas on September 23, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> It wound up grossing £245,422 ($786,021)<a href="/wiki/3D_film" title="3D film">3D</a> from 276 theaters, finishing at eleventh on the weekend box office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Two years later, the 20th anniversary of <i>Jurassic Park</i> led to a theatrical release of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3-D_film" title="3-D film">3-D version</a> of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Spielberg declared that he had produced the film with a sort of "subconscious 3D", as scenes feature animals walking toward the cameras and some effects of foreground and background overlay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usa_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-usa-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, he stated in an interview that <i>Jurassic Park</i> was the only of his works he had considered for a conversion,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> and once he saw the 3D version of <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> in 2012, he liked the new look of the film so much that he hired the same retrofitting company, Stereo D. Spielberg and cinematographer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Janusz_Kaminski" title="Janusz Kaminski">Janusz Kaminski</a> supervised the nine month process closely in-between the production of <i><a href="/wiki/Lincoln_(2012_film)" title="Lincoln (2012 film)">Lincoln</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usa_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-usa-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Stereo D vice-president Aaron Parry declared that the conversion was an evolution of what the company had done with <i>Titanic</i>, "being able to capitalize on everything we learned with <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron" title="James Cameron">Jim</a> on <i>Titanic</i> and take it into a different genre and movie, and one with so many technical achievements." The studio had the help of ILM, which contributed some elements and updated effects shots for a better visual enhancement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> It opened on the United States and seven other territories on April 5, 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> with other countries receiving the re-release in the following six months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-m2_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-m2-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Box office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Jurassic Park</i> became the highest grossing film released worldwide up to that time, beating Spielberg's <i><a href="/wiki/E.T._the_Extra-Terrestrial" title="E.T. the Extra-Terrestrial">E.T. the Extra-Terrestrial</a></i> which previously held the title (though it did not top <i>E.T.</i> in North America).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Following $3.1 million from midnight screenings on June 10, the film earned $47 million in its first weekend, with the $50.1 million total breaking the opening weekend record set by <i><a href="/wiki/Batman_Returns" title="Batman Returns">Batman Returns</a></i> the year before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opening_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-opening-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> By the end of its first week, <i>Jurassic Park</i> had grossed $81.7 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> and stayed at number one for three weeks. It eventually grossed $357 million in the U.S. and Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weekly_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-weekly-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> The film also did very well in international markets, breaking opening records in the United Kingdom, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> ultimately earning $914 million worldwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mojo_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-mojo-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> with Spielberg reportedly making over $250 million from the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Jurassic Park'</i>s worldwide gross was topped five years later by <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron" title="James Cameron">James Cameron</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The 3D re-release of <i>Jurassic Park</i> opened at fourth place in North America, with $18.6 million from 2,771 locations. <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> showings accounted for over $6 million, with the 32 percent being the highest IMAX share ever for a nationwide release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> The international release had its most successful weekend in the last week of August, when it managed to climb to the top of the overseas box office with a $28.8 million debut in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The reissue earned $45,385,935 in North America and $44,500,00 internationally as of August 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> leading to a lifetime gross of $402,453,882 in North America and $628,723,171 overseas, totaling up to a worldwide gross of $1,029,939,903. This makes <i>Jurassic Park</i> the 17th film to reach $1 billion and ranks it as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">15th highest-grossing film</a> of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mojo_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-mojo-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><span id="Reception"></span><span id="Critical_reception"></span><span id="Critics"></span></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response">Critical response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Critical response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Jurassic Park</i> received widespread critical acclaim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metacritic_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> High praise was heaped on the visual effects, although there was some criticism leveled at departures from the book. <a href="/wiki/Janet_Maslin" title="Janet Maslin">Janet Maslin</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> called it "a true movie milestone, presenting awe- and fear-inspiring sights never before seen on the screen... On paper, this story is tailor-made for Mr. Spielberg's talents...[but] [i]t becomes less crisp on screen than it was on the page, with much of the enjoyable jargon either mumbled confusingly or otherwise thrown away."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Travers" title="Peter Travers">Peter Travers</a> described the film as "colossal entertainment—the eye-popping, mind-bending, kick-out-the-jams thrill ride of summer and probably the year [...] Compared with the dinos, the characters are dry bones, indeed. Crichton and co-screenwriter David Koepp have flattened them into nonentities on the trip from page to screen."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> noted, "The movie delivers all too well on its promise to show us dinosaurs. We see them early and often, and they are indeed a triumph of special effects artistry, but the movie is lacking other qualities that it needs even more, such as a sense of awe and wonderment, and strong human story values."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Henry Sheehan argued, "The complaints over <i>Jurassic Park'</i>s lack of story and character sound a little off the point," pointing out the story arc of Grant learning to protect Hammond's grandchildren despite his initial dislike of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lack_of_story.3F_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-lack_of_story.3F-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine gave the film five stars,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (November 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> hailing it as "quite simply one of the greatest blockbusters of all time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">Review aggregation website</a> <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> retrospectively gave the film a "Certified Fresh" rating of 93% based on 111 reviews, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weighted_mean" title="Weighted mean">rating average</a> score of 8.2 out of 10. The site's consensus states "<i>Jurassic Park</i> is a spectacle of special effects and life-like animatronics, with some of Spielberg's best sequences of sustained awe and sheer terror since <i><a href="/wiki/Jaws_(film)" title="Jaws (film)">Jaws</a></i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a> gave the film a score of 68/100 based on reviews from 20 critics, indicating "generally favorable reviews".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metacritic_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Film_Institute_recognition"><a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute" title="American Film Institute">American Film Institute</a> recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: American Film Institute recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Movies_(10th_Anniversary_Edition)" title="AFI's 100 Years...100 Movies (10th Anniversary Edition)">AFI's 100 Years...100 Movies (10th Anniversary Edition)</a> – Nominated</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Movie_Quotes" title="AFI's 100 Years...100 Movie Quotes">AFI's 100 Years...100 Movie Quotes</a>:
<ul>
<li>"Life will find a way." – Nominated</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Thrills" title="AFI's 100 Years...100 Thrills">AFI's 100 Years...100 Thrills</a> – #35</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Movies" title="AFI's 100 Years...100 Movies">AFI's 100 Years...100 Movies</a> – Nominated</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span id="Awards"></span><span id="Accolades"></span> In March 1994, <i>Jurassic Park</i> won all three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a> it was nominated for: <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound_Editing" title="Academy Award for Best Sound Editing">Best Sound Editing</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound_Mixing" title="Academy Award for Best Sound Mixing">Best Sound Mixing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects" title="Academy Award for Best Visual Effects">Best Visual Effects</a> (at the same ceremony, Spielberg, editor Michael Kahn and composer John Williams won Academy Awards for <i>Schindler's List</i>). The film won honors outside the U.S. including the 1994 <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">BAFTA</a> for <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Special_Visual_Effects" title="BAFTA Award for Best Special Visual Effects">Best Special Effects</a>, as well as the Award for the Public's Favorite Film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> It won the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award" title="Hugo Award">Hugo Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award_for_Best_Dramatic_Presentation" title="Hugo Award for Best Dramatic Presentation">Best Dramatic Presentation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> and the 1993 <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award" title="Saturn Award">Saturn Awards</a> for <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Science_Fiction_Film" title="Saturn Award for Best Science Fiction Film">Best Science Fiction Film</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Saturn Award for Best Director">Best Direction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Writing" title="Saturn Award for Best Writing">Best Writing</a> for Crichton and Koepp and <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Special_Effects" title="Saturn Award for Best Special Effects">Best Special Effects</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sat_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-sat-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> The film won the 1993 <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards" title="People's Choice Awards">People's Choice Awards</a> for Favorite All-Around Motion Picture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Young_Artist_Award" title="Young Artist Award">Young Artist Awards</a> were given to Ariana Richards and Joseph Mazzello, with the film winning an Outstanding Action/Adventure Family Motion Picture award.<sup class="reference"
