<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jurassic_Park_Discovery_Centre.jpg"><img alt='The gateway to a facility reading "Jurassic Park" at the top, "Discovery Center" at the bottom, and a rocky panel with a Tyrannosaurus skeleton in-between.' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1707" data-file-width="1280" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Jurassic_Park_Discovery_Centre.jpg/220px-Jurassic_Park_Discovery_Centre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Jurassic_Park_Discovery_Centre.jpg/330px-Jurassic_Park_Discovery_Centre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Jurassic_Park_Discovery_Centre.jpg/440px-Jurassic_Park_Discovery_Centre.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jurassic_Park_Discovery_Centre.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Entrance to the Jurassic Park Discovery Center at <a href="/wiki/Islands_of_Adventure" title="Islands of Adventure">Islands of Adventure</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the years following its release, <i>Jurassic Park</i> has frequently been cited by film critics and industry professionals as one of the greatest movies of the action and thriller genres. The <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute" title="American Film Institute">American Film Institute</a> named <i>Jurassic Park</i> the 35th most thrilling film of all time on June 13, 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Film_Critics_Association" title="Chicago Film Critics Association">Chicago Film Critics Association</a> also ranked <i>Jurassic Park</i> as the 55th scariest movie of all time and, in 2005, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bravo_(US_TV_channel)" title="Bravo (US TV channel)">Bravo</a> chose the scene in which Lex and Tim are stalked by two raptors in the kitchen as the 95th scariest movie moment ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> On <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine's fifteenth anniversary in 2004, it judged <i>Jurassic Park</i> the sixth most influential film of the magazine's lifetime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-influence_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-influence-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> called the first encounter with a <i>Brachiosaurus</i> the 28th most magical moment in cinema.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, an <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> poll of readers, filmmakers, and critics also rated it one of the 500 greatest films of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> On <i><a href="/wiki/Film_Review_(magazine)" title="Film Review (magazine)">Film Review</a></i> '​s fifty-fifth anniversary in 2005, it declared the film to be one of the five most important in the magazine's lifetime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006, <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> ranked <i>Jurassic Park</i> as the 19th greatest film franchise ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> In a 2010 poll, the readers of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> rated it the greatest summer movie of the previous 20 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> The popularity of the movie caused the management of the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> expansion franchise founded in Toronto in 1995 to adopt the nickname <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Raptors" title="Toronto Raptors">Raptors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-raph_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-raph-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The biggest impact <i>Jurassic Park</i> had on subsequent films regarded Industrial Light and Magic's computer-generated visual effects. Film historian <a href="/wiki/Tom_Shone" title="Tom Shone">Tom Shone</a> commented on the film's innovation and influence, saying that "In its way, <i>Jurassic Park</i> heralded a revolution in movies as profound as the coming of sound in 1927."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> Many filmmakers saw <i>Jurassic Park</i> '​s effects as a realization that many of their visions, previously thought unfeasible or too expensive, were now possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-influence_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-influence-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> ILM owner <a href="/wiki/George_Lucas" title="George Lucas">George Lucas</a>, realizing the success of creating realistic live dinosaurs by his own company, started to make the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> prequels,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Kubrick" title="Stanley Kubrick">Stanley Kubrick</a> decided to invest in pet project <i><a href="/wiki/A.I._Artificial_Intelligence" title="A.I. Artificial Intelligence">A.I. Artificial Intelligence</a></i>, to which he would later bring Spielberg to direct,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-influence_129-2"><a href="#cite_note-influence-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">Peter Jackson</a> began to re-explore his childhood love of <a href="/wiki/Fantasy_film" title="Fantasy film">fantasy films</a>, a path that led him to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)" title="The Lord of the Rings (film series)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(2005_film)" title="King Kong (2005 film)">King Kong</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Jurassic Park</i> has also inspired films and documentaries with dinosaurs such as the American adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/Godzilla_(1998_film)" title="Godzilla (1998 film)">Godzilla</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Carnosaur_(film)" title="Carnosaur (film)">Carnosaur</a></i> (in which Laura Dern's mother <a href="/wiki/Diane_Ladd" title="Diane Ladd">Diane Ladd</a> starred) and <i><a href="/wiki/Walking_with_Dinosaurs" title="Walking with Dinosaurs">Walking with Dinosaurs</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-influence_129-3"><a href="#cite_note-influence-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> Stan Winston, enthusiastic about the new technology pioneered by the film, joined with <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> and director <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron" title="James Cameron">James Cameron</a> to form a new special effects company, <a href="/wiki/Digital_Domain" title="Digital Domain">Digital Domain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequels_and_merchandise">Sequels and merchandise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sequels and merchandise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_(franchise)" title="Jurassic Park (franchise)">Jurassic Park (franchise)</a></div>
<p>After the enormous success of the film, Spielberg requested Michael Crichton to write a sequel novel, leading to the 1995 book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lost_World_(Crichton_novel)" title="The Lost World (Crichton novel)">The Lost World</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> which in turn was adapted as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lost_World:_Jurassic_Park" title="The Lost World: Jurassic Park">The Lost World: Jurassic Park</a></i> in 1997, also directed by Spielberg and written by David Koepp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Another film, <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_III" title="Jurassic Park III">Jurassic Park III</a></i>, was released on 2001 under the direction of <a href="/wiki/Joe_Johnston" title="Joe Johnston">Joe Johnston</a> and Spielberg as executive producer, featuring an original script that still incorporated unused elements from Crichton's original <i>Jurassic Park</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> A fourth installment <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_World" title="Jurassic World">Jurassic World</a></i> is currently under production, with a June 12, 2015 release date. Spielberg again only produces, with <a href="/wiki/Colin_Trevorrow" title="Colin Trevorrow">Colin Trevorrow</a> directing a script written by himself and <a href="/wiki/Derek_Connolly" title="Derek Connolly">Derek Connolly</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The story of the film was also continued in auxiliary media, at times even unattached to the film sequels themselves. These included a series of <i>Jurassic Park</i> <a href="/wiki/Comic_book" title="Comic book">comic books</a> written by <a href="/wiki/Steve_Englehart" title="Steve Englehart">Steve Englehart</a> for <a href="/wiki/Topps_Comics" title="Topps Comics">Topps Comics</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> and video games such as Ocean Software's <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_2:_The_Chaos_Continues" title="Jurassic Park 2: The Chaos Continues">Jurassic Park 2: The Chaos Continues</a></i> (1994), <a href="/wiki/Vivendi" title="Vivendi">Vivendi</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park:_Operation_Genesis" title="Jurassic Park: Operation Genesis">Jurassic Park: Operation Genesis</a></i> (2003) and <a href="/wiki/Telltale_Games" title="Telltale Games">Telltale Games</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park:_The_Game" title="Jurassic Park: The Game">Jurassic Park: The Game</a></i> (2011).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-games_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-games-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>All of the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Parks_%26_Resorts" title="Universal Parks &amp; Resorts">Universal Parks &amp; Resorts</a> include a <i>Jurassic Park</i>-themed ride. The first was <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park:_The_Ride_(Universal_Studios_Hollywood)" title="Jurassic Park: The Ride (Universal Studios Hollywood)">Jurassic Park: The Ride</a> at Universal Studios Hollywood on June 15, 1996, built after six years of development at a cost of $110 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-studiotour_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-studiotour-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> Said attraction was replicated on <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios_Japan" title="Universal Studios Japan">Universal Studios Japan</a> in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Islands_of_Adventure" title="Islands of Adventure">Islands of Adventure</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orlando" title="Orlando">Orlando</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, has an entire section of the park dedicated to <i>Jurassic Park</i> that includes the main ride, christened "Jurassic Park River Adventure", and many smaller rides and attractions based on the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios_Singapore" title="Universal Studios Singapore">Universal Studios Singapore</a>, opened in 2010, the Themed Zone named The Lost World consists mostly of <i>Jurassic Park</i> rides, such as the roller coaster <a href="/wiki/Canopy_Flyer" title="Canopy Flyer">Canopy Flyer</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_rafting_ride" title="River rafting ride">river rapids</a> <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_Rapids_Adventure" title="Jurassic Park Rapids Adventure">Jurassic Park Rapids Adventure</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The film made its <a href="/wiki/VHS" title="VHS">VHS</a> and <a href="/wiki/LaserDisc" title="LaserDisc">LaserDisc</a> debut on October 4, 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> With 17 million units sold in both formats,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Jurassic Park</i> is the fifth best-selling VHS tape ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Jurassic Park</i> was first released on <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> on October 10, 2000, in both a stand-alone disk, and in a box set along with sequel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lost_World:_Jurassic_Park" title="The Lost World: Jurassic Park">The Lost World: Jurassic Park</a></i> and both movies' soundtrack albums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> It ended as the 13th best-selling DVD of 2000 counting both versions, finishing the year with 910,000 units sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the release of <i>Jurassic Park III</i>, a new box set with all films called <i>Jurassic Park Trilogy</i> was released on December 11, 2001, it was re-released on VHS and DVD as part of its 15th anniversary on 8 October 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> It was repackaged as <i>Jurassic Park Adventure Pack</i> on November 29, 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The trilogy was released on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a> on October 25, 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> debuting at fifth on the Blu-ray charts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> and being nominated as the best release of the year by both the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Film_Critics_Society_Awards" title="Las Vegas Film Critics Society Awards">Las Vegas Film Critics Society</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LasVegas_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-LasVegas-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award" title="Saturn Award">Saturn Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, <i>Jurassic Park</i> was among 25 films Universal picked for a box set that celebrated the studio's 100th anniversary,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> while also receiving a standalone 100th anniversary Blu-ray featuring an <a href="/wiki/Augmented_reality" title="Augmented reality">augmented reality</a> cover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> The following year, the 20th anniversary 3D conversion was issued on Blu-ray 3D.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurassic_Park_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
